<div id="review_1011966298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011966298" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11726668-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354652002p2/11726668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011966298?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/11726668-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1011966298&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011966298" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7478774035797386722">First off, please do not attempt to bicker or engage me in an argument about my opinion of this book. I have my opinion, you have yours—if you liked the book, then by all means go write up a glowing review expressing your positive thoughts—you're entitled to share them, just as I am entitled to share my negative ones. <br/><br/>No real spoilers, just lots of disappointment follow. If I could have rated it lower than one star, I would have.<br/><br/>As a longtime fan of the VA world since its inception, I had a lot </span>
  <span id="freeText7478774035797386722" style="display:none">First off, please do not attempt to bicker or engage me in an argument about my opinion of this book. I have my opinion, you have yours—if you liked the book, then by all means go write up a glowing review expressing your positive thoughts—you're entitled to share them, just as I am entitled to share my negative ones. <br /><br />No real spoilers, just lots of disappointment follow. If I could have rated it lower than one star, I would have.<br /><br />As a longtime fan of the VA world since its inception, I had a lot of hopes for the spinoff series. That hope has dimmed more and more with each book after The Golden Lily; Silver Shadows killed it completely.<br />I used to genuinely like Sydney Sage—back when she was an interesting character that drew the reader in. I haven't seen that character in a long, long time.<br /><br />TBH, I didn't think Sydney could become any more of a Mary Sue... but she did. I suppose its normal for someone who has experienced months of torture to come out with no PTSD other than a fear of the dark... that fits right in with her eating disorder that was healed in a week just because the hot guy said it wasn't cute and her banishing the teachings and moral beliefs that had been drummed into her since birth over a week or two. <br /><br />To make matters worse Adrian had now become a Gary Stu, so out of character that I don't even recognize the charming dreamwalker we all fell in love with in VA. All that character growth that Sydney supposedly inspired in him? The loss of selfishness and being more mature? Yeah he really displays that when he just expects everyone to accept what he's done (you'll know it when you read it) and doesn't give a fu--crap that he's putting Lissa—who is ALREADY in a precarious position—in a situation she cannot win. Yeahhh... way to show how much he's grown. Excellent job there.<br /><br />Add to that the fact that Rose is no longer written showing the character growth and maturity she gained through the last two books of the VA series—she's been written to correspond with the flop of a movie, so now she acts like a twelve year old. I mean seriously.... hanging upside down in a chair? This is the Queens PRIMARY GUARDIAN we are talking about... as well as being a member of the elite Royal guard. This is the WOMAN who stood up to the man she loved more than anything—who she had chased half way around the world—and was mature enough to say: 'You have to forgive yourself. For real. Everyone else has. If you can't, then you can't go on either. We can't.ʺ Now...in one SINGLE IDIOTIC SENTENCE MAKING HER ACT LIKE A FRIGGING CHILD... all that growth was erased. <br /><br />It's one thing to show subtle character growth—that's a good, positive thing. It's something else entirely to decimate the characters personalities to the point the reader is left starting at the page wondering who the hell the character is and not liking the new verion of them one little bit. <br /><br />Oh and let's not forget that the main reason Jill was sent to Palm Springs was because it was in the middle of the desert and as such there was a low Moroi presence in the surrounding area. Now we learn that there's a small hidden ACADEMY in NEVADA—which is a) the middle of the desert and b) just a few hours car ride away. Guess no one was worried any of the Moroi/dhampirs that worked at this Academy/Parents visiting students—etc— might decide to weekend in Palm Springs. <br /><br />Where the Dragomir Princess was HIDING OUT. <br /><br />I guess they just... forgot about this Academy? It must be REALLY well hidden!<br /><br /><br />All in all, I'm glad the series is coming to an end. The Golden Lily was the last book that wasn't ooc—every book after that has just gone more and more downhill. It's almost like Richelle has lost her inspiration and no longer connects with the characters—either that or someone is ghostwriting for her and isn't even bothering to attempt to try to stick with the character's personalities as they were originally written. <br /><br />Namaste<br />—sws<br /><br />*excuse typos as it is 4 AM and I just can't be bothered to fix 'em.*</span>
  <a data-text-id="7478774035797386722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AHUpNdk+VKbuIak5j8NCI7NIBO2zLw6Ssh4E54xIzJE6U0DnYmCdzkkKHVh4Nkj8ZRfjJX2igPXpYEJWQQs+Cw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yHhGnJHVmh5OkeR8bxYZzIfBqHfAB7kI/8mCU8c3TrvyXi9OKotTdum6UB2Y4xMTUZ5Pvw6KN2+kt8TiCnS8IQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6471348240050938647">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br/><br/>A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away f</span>
  <span id="freeText6471348240050938647" style="display:none">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br /><br />A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away from books (either reading or writing them), she enjoys bad reality TV, traveling, trying interesting cocktails, and shopping for dresses. She's a self-professed coffee addict and has a passion for all things wacky and humorous.<br /></span>
